<user>117828169108326646114<//user><Gmap_id>0x808fec68980983c7:0xaf448f3a34cb28ea< /Gmap_id>< Text>
I get my haircut here all the time. They are perfect for a quick and cheap haircut (they are the cheapest in terms of the price that I've found). You can get an additional discount/coupon on the back of your Safeway receipt. So why the 3 stars? The pros are that it is fast and affordable and the guy who cuts my hair (Sonny - I go to the same person every time) does a decent and consistent job. The cons are that the ambience, service, and professionalism (or lack thereof) are consistently reflective of the price point... low budget. The ambience is busy, loud, and crowded. The service is fast, inattentive, and resembles the DMV. The lack of professionalism indicates that you will not be greeted properly or warmly, you will have to take a number and wait till your number is called, the stylists don't speak english very well making comunicating your desired hairstyle challenging, and they will speak in their own language directly in front of you and not give a damn about it, making for a very uncomfortable situation to be in. Btw, I speak a language(s) other than English as well, so nothing negative about other languages, ethnicities, or cultures... just complaining about the lack of ettiquettes involved.</Text>

< Review>
I've been swimming on an adult club team at this pool for three years. The aquatics facility is beautiful, the coaching staff is great and I love swimming with others.  The pool is not open to the general public, so I'm glad I found a program that has a permit, the only one! The pool also has a hot tub where you can relax after a long set. The other swimmers are friendly, the locker rooms are clean; it is overall a great experience.< /Review>

< text>
Stopped by really quick. I've noticed driving by this truck is always busy. Decided to stop today and grab a taco. I got an asada taco with verde, be warned the verde is a little on the spicy side so if you're sensitive to spices you might not like the sauce, I on the other hand love spicy food. A taco and a bottled coke (the real stuff) was $6. Not a bad deal for a quick lunch. Plus the ladies are super friendly and they have a seating area set up right next to the truck if you wanna eat there.<//text>

< review>
Favorite jazz venue hands down (of all of California). The caliber of artists that come thru on a regular basis is amazing, and it‚Äôs not a coincidence why that is the case. The staff and owner have a deep appreciation for music and it is reflected by the atmosphere of the room. The drink selection ranges from 8-13 usually, with some nightly specials that are pretty nice. I have yet to try the food but they do look and smell tempting when they come by.

Overall, an intimate and wonderfully sounding venue that is worth a visit.

Pictured: artists Pedro Martins and Louis Cole.< /review>

< Review>
It's great to have a venue that plays live jazz right in the heart of DTLA. The place is located on the 3rd floor in a little plaza in the NE corner.
It can be a little confusing to find the first time.
There seems to be plenty of street parking past a certain hour when most concerts are taking place.
I live close by so I always Uber it.
Their calendar is consistently full will different jazz bands.
Entrance was $15 for students (either ID or email works as proof, as long as u prove ur a student), or $20 general entrance fees.

$13 for a Malbec which I think gets the job done.
I walked in late, but the music lasts a pretty good amount of time. It starts at 9:15pm, but seems to usually end around 11:30/midnight-ish...
They got some good artwork too.<//Review>

<Review>Great live music here for jazz enthusiasts in a hidden gem in a mall in Little Tokio. This place is awesome but it's meant for serious music listeners. This is not a place to talk to your friends/date with background music: come here if you want to actively listen to some great musicians in a relatively intimate setting. The place itself is a decent size with a bar to the left upon entering the front door, which then led to seating area and stage. 5< /rate>
< Review>
Many of the reviews here are clearly about other places with similar names; the guy who thinks it's in the Gaslamp District must have had a few on the 120-mile cab ride.  This is a serious jazz club in Little Tokyo, Los Angeles.  It's theme is not tiki or speakeasy, but "genteel jazz club that has blue furniture."  They serve bar food but not meals.  If you come here on a casual date, you are not getting anywhere unless she really likes jazz.   This is the kind of place where casual conversation during performances is not really appropriate.

Often has USC grad student acts, classical-jazz fusion, and other innovative stuff.  Clientele of serious jazz fans.

Many of the seats are uncomfortable, so get there early if you have back problems or mobility issues.  It's hard to find, on the third floor of a (nice) minimall.  Near LT Gold Line stop and walkable from Union Station red/purple line, but the Metro closes before the endtime of most shows.  (Hey, Joon, I'd come to your place once a week if the show times were 90 minutes earlier!)<//Review>

< review>
This is one of my favorite speakeasies/bars of all time. Everything is totally tiki, and the bar itself is themed like a pirate ship. You can watch the bartenders toss one obscure ingredient after another into your drink, creating a masterfully crafted cocktail sure to transport you straight into an 1800's Caribbean.

Last night was my second visit. I ordered one of my favorite drinks, Lei Lani Nouveau (interesting and well-balanced, but sweet -- skip if you don't like sugar!). After taking a few sips, another bar-goer knocked it out of my hand, and the (mostly full) glass shattered on the floor. Three employees hurried over to sweep and mop up the mess, each one instructing my boyfriend and me not to try to help to protect our hands from broken glass. We apologized and thanked them for helping. Right as the last employee was finishing cleaning up our mess, a bartender brought over a perfect new Lei Lani Nouveau and handed it to me, telling me not to worry about it. Not only did we not have to ask for a new drink, they didn't even have to ask me what I'd ordered to remake it! They handled it so professionally and kindly, five minutes after losing my drink they'd totally erased the situation.</review>

< review>
Advertised price per gallon for diesel was 3.78 per gallonon May 24, 2021, as noted on their billboard. I paid at the pump with a debit card and spoke with the manager to correct the price. The manager told me to wait until after I pumped and to push the debit button, but there wasn't one. I went back into the store to remedy the problem, and she said it rung it up as credit and there was nothing she could do about it. I told her they were not advertising the right price and it's a shame they lost my business forever for a mere $2.50.<//review>

<gmap_id>0x80ecd7a8385c9d67:0xf73b71472253114b</gmap_id><pictures>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNoP8AdOCshfl3Y6DUZH-Wl3vvhyNCfOmn-KoMp=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNuDZd1JrFm1K_uwP_Egxbz2VS0L77oV8j9-TLf=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]< /pictures>< review>
Whalebone is a great small winery.  We were fortunate to get a reservation on short notice (thank you!!).  The winery offers a very chill and relaxed environment, almost to the point you forget you're at a winery.  While you are still educated on the wine, all pretentiousness is eliminated.  They do it right in terms of appealing to all wine drinkers, especially those who may be new to the world of wine.  Our tasting menu offered seven options, at $15/per person,  and all were easy drinking.   We ended up selecting two bottles, but know it was a struggle to only pick two!  The labels are also untraditional of most wineries - think bold, fun, super colorful.
I highly recommend a visit to Whalebone during your trip.< /review>

<user_id>117467885232868884370</user_id>< Name>
Judy A</Name>
<time>1593792263600<//time>< rate>
5< /rate>
< Text>
Whalebone Winery is a treasured find along the plethora of tasting rooms in Paso Robles.   I consistently like all of their wines which is a rarity given that there are plenty of wineries that are at the other end of the spectrum.   The tasting room is an intimate and cozy affair run warmly by a kind, and knowledgeable family.  The outdoor picnic area boasts a sumptuous view of rolling vineyard hills and is staffed by an adorable English bulldog named Bentley who is honored on one of Whalebone's labels.  Whalebone Winery ranks high on my list of favorite California wineries.   It's offerings are delectable and reasonably priced.   I'm surprised this winery doesn't get more buzz, but I sense that it is only a matter of time before it is more widely discovered.   I highly recommend a visit to WW.<//Text>

<text>We stopped here because of the name, but we did really like their wines.  The have a long history, but mostly as a hobby for the first decade or two.  At that time they were known as Bob Wine....because Bob made it.   At that time, they primary sold their grapes, while making some wine for themselves and a small amount for others.  When they decided to make it an official winery, they chose the name Whalebone, for the whale bones found when planting.  We really liked their Cabs.  They have a limited selection of wines, but what they have are worth the stop.< /text>< pictures>

<rating>3<//rating>< Text>
To start with the positives, the hotel is located closely to the center of downtown Casriloga, so is very easy to get to nearby restaurants. The pool, fed by natural mineral water from hot springs is also very comfortable and enjoyable to swim in. However, there were a few negatives from the stay. When we got to the hotel, the showers were not working at all, as they were working to fix the hot water heater. The staff had no good solutions but to wait for them to fix it sometime that day. Definitely a big concern given that we needed to get ready for a wedding that afternoon. Fortunately it was fixed in time, though still a big inconvenience. Overall there was also a lot of construction going on, and made the place look a little messy. I'm sure in some time the place will be a great stay, but may need some time to finish renovations.</Text>

<name>John Economides<//name>< Date>
1478094178721</Date>
<rating>2</rating>< text>
From the outside, this hotel appears to be "quaint". But once you actually get inside your room, you find that it's no different from your run of the mill 20 year old Holiday Inn.
Discolored paint, peeling wall paper, a bathroom that has clearly had a thorough using. Air conditioning unit that still has unit mounted controls. Light bulbs that long ago ceased to be color matched (daylight or soft white people, it's not hard).

There are a few stars here, the bedside alarm clock is completely dimmable to the no light position while retaining alarm functionality. That same clock also has two edison outlets and two USB outlets for charging gadgets. Enough that I didn't have to worry about unpacking my travel power strip.

There's a dorm room sized refrigerator in the room. And a Safeway a mere 8 miles away. There's a microwave in the lobby... but that brings me to my next detraction.

The lobby is only staffed/open from 7AM-10PM. They start serving breakfast at 7AM, so I am curious why the lobby isn't open an hour prior to that. Much less staffed and open 24HR regardless.

I'm only a day in, so I'm sure there will be more things I notice in the coming week. If you're listening, Choice Hotels... you should consider changing your brand standards.</text>

< Review>
The usual Panera fare... with a few positive notes: 1) it's now very easy to tip the staff right at the POS card reader. Good move, Panera management! 2) had a new offering-- Modern Greek Salad. Very refreshing. Much less sodium than the "classic" Greek salad. Not overly dressed. And preyy filling with addition of quinoa (only 14 grams Carbohydrate for the half salad); 3) my order was wrong, but the staffer I informed of the error was so eager to please. I had my correct order by the time I had dropped off my wife's meal.

Will be checking several new offerings and updating this review over the next month or so.< /Review>

<username>BD</username><rate>4<//rate><Resp>None<//Resp>< Text>
Anybody with some cash can buy a franchise. But remember, employees can make it work or break it! And the only way your going to pick out the gems during the interviewing process is by experiencing the hiring process for a few years. And then, you'll most likely have a well tuned and profitable franchise!
I say this only because I listened to a customer complain to a manager about the disrespect they got from one of the employees.
Look, making a franchise profitable isn't easy! If it was, do you think the selling company would actually be selling them to you, or keeping all of the locations as corporate owned and operated? They want you to invest YOUR money so YOU have a vested interest to make the business successful! And I totally get that.
Average employees treat your business like aa renter treats your property! This is why management that hires and runs a retail business knows that they are just well-paid babysitters!
So the lesson is: Hire a manager that knows how to A) Hire good people, and B) Manage good people in a way that they like going to work and want to stay!
Statistically, the food business already is doomed from the beginning. A lot of competitors, a lot of employees just looking for ways to milk the job and steal you blind. Sorry, that's the truth of the matter.
When the customer has way too many choices for dining out, it just takes one bad experience with an untrained and uncaring employee to lose the customer for good.
Assistant Managers, keep your ears open and mostly just listen. Listen to what the customers are willing to share with you, and most of all listen to what the employees are saying to each other. That's where a good assistant manager earns his or her pay. Reward the good employees and don't be afraid to let the not so good ones go. Because bad attitude is like a cancer when it comes down to spreading from one employee to another!!< /Text>

<pics>None</pics><time>1522188984636< /time><Name>April Battaglia< /Name>< Review>
Over $33 for mac and cheese, a salad, smoothie and two coffees.  The food just isn't that good.  Outside, the trashcans were over-flowing and piled up with dirty dishes. The location was littered with debris iside the first set of doors.  Inside the ordering area, the floor was sticky.  The young woman taking my order did not know the menu, or understand that "non-dairy" means no dairy products.  Yogurt is dairy.  I ordered the peach blueberry with almond milk smoothie.  That's literally the name of the smoothie under the "non-dairy smoothie" heading: "peach blueberry w/almond milk" and is listed at $4.69.  I was charged $.50 extra for the almond milk.  My daughter ordered iced coffee and was told she would get a cup of ice for the iced coffee dispenser.  She was given an empty cup, no ice, and there is no ice at the coffee bar.  We figured out on our own she had to walk to the other side of the restaurant to use the ice dispenser and then go back to the coffee bar, and then walk back over to pick up the order. I don't mind paying for good food, the extra $.50 won't kill me, and I like walking.   The problem is that the whole time, I was spoken too as if I was the one who didn't understand what was going on, and the mistakes were my fault.  Twice the manager asked if we were okay and offered us pastries for our troubles.  Pastries will never make up for eyes rolling at me, pre-prepared and over-priced dishes, the hair in the ceasar salad, or negative attitudes.  Thanks, but I will never be back. To any Panera.  I'm glad your parent company, Starbucks, is closing your locations.  One.  By.  One.< /Review>

My daughter ordered iced coffee and was told she would get a cup of ice for the iced coffee dispenser.  She was given an empty cup, no ice, and there is no ice at the coffee bar.  We figured out on our own she had to walk to the other side of the restaurant to use the ice dispenser and then go back to the coffee bar, and then walk back over to pick up the order. I don't mind paying for good food, the extra $.50 won't kill me, and I like walking.   The problem is that the whole time, I was spoken too as if I was the one who didn't understand what was going on, and the mistakes were my fault.  Twice the manager asked if we were okay and offered us pastries for our troubles.  Pastries will never make up for eyes rolling at me, pre-prepared and over-priced dishes, the hair in the ceasar salad, or negative attitudes.  Thanks, but I will never be back. To any Panera.  I'm glad your parent company, Starbucks, is closing your locations.  One.  By.  One.<//Review>
